## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology
**Analysis**: The task models instantaneous population growth rate as a function of time and current population size, a core problem in mathematical biology and theoretical ecology that captures how births, deaths, resource competition, and environmental fluctuations shape population trajectories over time.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (Unrestricted proportional population increase)
- Density-dependent mortality: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**2 (Linear birth rate offset by quadratic intraspecific competition)
- Beverton-Holt continuous dynamics: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (Saturating recruitment with density-dependent survival)
- Gompertz growth model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 - c2 * log(P)) (Decelerating growth approaching an asymptotic limit)
- Theta-logistic model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P**c2) (Generalized nonlinear density dependence)
- Weak Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (c1 + P) * (c2 - P) (Reduced per-capita growth at low densities without extinction threshold)
- Strong Allee effect: dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (c2 - P) (Critical population threshold below which growth becomes negative)
- Ricker-type continuous approximation: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * P) (Overcompensatory density dependence with peak recruitment)
- Seasonal forcing model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) (Periodic environmental modulation of baseline growth rate)
- Allometric vital rate balance: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c1 * P**c2 (Power-law scaling of resource acquisition versus metabolic maintenance)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope â†’ Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects â†’ Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay â†’ Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior â†’ Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects â†’ Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-dependent per-capita regulation â†’ dP_dt/P is a monotonically decreasing function of P
- Allee threshold dynamics â†’ dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (c2 - P) with positive roots creating unstable equilibrium
- Overcompensatory recruitment â†’ dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(-c1 * P) or high-degree polynomials peaking at intermediate P
- Seasonal environmental modulation â†’ dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) multiplying baseline growth
- Metabolic scaling of vital rates â†’ dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c1 * P**c2 balancing acquisition and maintenance exponents
- Bounded asymptotic trajectories â†’ dP_dt â†’ 0 as P â†’ c1, ensuring finite population size via rational or polynomial damping
- Exploitation/harvesting pressure â†’ dP_dt = natural_growth - c0, shifting equilibrium via constant subtraction
- Nonlinear competition intensity â†’ dP_dt contains P**n (n>1) terms where exponent reflects spatial clustering or resource partitioning
